### Post by abhilashmhaisne on 2014-11-28
I have a dell inspiron laptop with ubuntu 14.04. Earlier my wifi used to work properly, however after some ap-hotspot scripts i tried, my wifi is not working. I uninstalled all scripts, still nothing. Here is the wireless.sh script in the other thread, which generated the wireless.txt file, for information about wireless. PLEASE HELP !!!
[ATTACH]258255[/ATTACH]

---

### Post by jeremy31 on 2014-11-28
Welcome to the forum


The first thing to do is remove a couple entries in /etc/modules with the text editor```
gksudo gedit /etc/modules
``` delete the second coretemp entry and brcmsmac save and exit program.  Reboot and run the script again ```
./wireless_script
```

---

### Post by abhilashmhaisne on 2014-11-28
Thank you. I did what you said, and here is the wireless.txt after rebooting.[ATTACH]258261[/ATTACH]

---

### Post by jeremy31 on 2014-11-28
For some reason the wl driver is loaded with no sign of a wifi device it will support, so it should be removed ```
sudo apt-get purge bcmwl-kernel-source broadcom-sta-common
```
Reboot again with the ethernet cable unplugged and see if you can connect using wifi

### Post by Hadaka on 2014-11-29
Hi,prior to your wifi NOT working, were you using a "hotspot"
then? Or were you just messing about with hotspot and things
got strange?

---

### Post by abhilashmhaisne on 2014-11-29
Prior to wifi not working, my my wifi worked (:P) , and i installed a script called ap-hotspot , which converted my ethernet connection into an access point hotspot. Now, after few days i removed that script(it was buggy), and since then, my wifi stopped working.

---

### Post by jeremy31 on 2014-11-29
> **abhilashmhaisne said:**
> Prior to wifi not working, my my wifi worked (:P) , and i installed a script called ap-hotspot , which converted my ethernet connection into an access point hotspot. Now, after few days i removed that script(it was buggy), and since then, my wifi stopped working.

I think the entries that were made by the hotspot program still remain, to erase the obvious one ```
sudo rm /etc/NetworkManager/system-connections/Hotspot
```
the second one can be eliminated with ```
sudo rm "/etc/NetworkManager/system-connections/New 802-11-wireless connection-9b68c448-1a00-4d9f-8f89-3d909ddda5f7"
```
then you might wifi after restarting network manager or rebooting computer

---
